in Penny-warths, and makes a very

than many- who now a-days pretend »to

of it, it the Proverb ſpeak truch, that bought Wit is

Hieraclitus 'Ridens.
{clling of theſe dear Penny-worths) I proteſt I do

not intend to make any advantage of you, but on-
ly to keep the Trade going in this dead time, by

turning the Penny. Here's one, there's t'other,
which 15 fair play between two Brothers. And if
vou have not your Penny-worth of Wit, I aſſure
you FI make it out in Honeſty, which at this time
is ſo very dear and ſcarce a Commodity, that ſome
think the Eaſi-India, others the Turkey-Company,
have tranſported moſt of it out of the Nation,
with the Good old Gold, as being of more intrin-
lick Value. | |
However, tis but t'other Penny; and you have
been ſo uſed to this Impoſt or Exciſe upon Fo-
reign and Domeſtick Intelligence, Votes, Petitions,
Speeches, c. that it would be a Grievance, and
againſt the Liberty of the Subject, to deprive you of
the pleature of having your Pockets pick'd, and

{cratching this Athenian Itch. My Defign is great

and generous, nothing leſs I aſſure you than the
publick Good, in earneſt, and to prevent Miſtakes
and falſe News, and to give you a true Information
of the State of things, and advance your Under-
{tandings above the common Rate of Coffee-houſe
Stateſmen, who think themſelves wiſer than the
Privy-Council, or, the Sages of the Law, when in
truth they are only fit to make Senators of Goatham
to hedge in a Cuckow, or drown an Fel. |
No that I may mingle Advantage and Diverſion,
I ſhall put my Diſcourſe into ſeveral Dreſſes, for I
know you. love variety, and know better things
than to cat Peaſe-Porridge cold nine days old, and
theretore you ſhall have ſeveral Scenes.

Enter Queries, Doubts and Scruples. Theſe are a
ſort of troubleſom Gentlemen which will croud
themſelves into all Cumpanies, and 'many times
ſpoil good Converſation; and I proteſt I could not
reſt from their Importunities till I had undertaken
ro make you acquainted with them. How you

will like them I cannot tell, but they fay they are

Loyalty ? | |

nour being ſince come to the Eſtate ? And whether

- Advertiſements.

| Hereas ſeveral Quacks of Gontham-College
have of late ſet out Bills, pretending an in-
fallible Cure for the Ague of the State, which by
Experience is found to endanger the putting their
Patients into a Fever, and the principal Ingredient
is the Jeſuits Powder of Toleration : Theſe are to
give Notice, that there is a cheap Medicine to be

| had, which will effectually do it; and for the pub-

lick Good, it is communicated in this time of In-
tection, and is as tollows. 3

Take of the Powder of Experience, rightly pre-
pared by Mr. Wiſeman, an Ounce; of true Primi-
tive Chriſtian Obedience, Conſideration, Gratitude,
Intereſt, Loyalty, and Allegiauce, of each halt 2
Pound; mingle them S. A. and take every Morning
and Evening a Doſe of it. You cannot err in the
quantity; and drink after it a Glaſs of Pump Royal,
and it will certainly preferve Health, or reſtore it.
Irs Virtues are theſe, it cures Dizzineſs, and the Me-
grim, or the running Round in the Head, cleanſes
the Blood from any Contagion of Sedition or Re-
bellion, cures the Scurvy, ſweetens the Breath,
comforts the Heart and the Head, makes a Man
chcarful, and live as much in Seven Years, as Neſtor
did in Three hundred. =
